  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7e343e20-f28c-4463-a6fd-6ba5b8dce731'
      });

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText3990051858306196577" style="display:none"><b>From global phenomenon C. S. Pacat comes the first in her critically acclaimed trilogy—with a bonus story.</b><br /><br />Damen is a warrior hero to his people, and the rightful heir to the throne of Akielos. But when his half brother seizes power, Damen is captured, stripped of his identity, and sent to serve the prince of an enemy nation as a pleasure slave.<br /><br />Beautiful, manipulative, and deadly, his new master, Prince Laurent, epitomizes the worst of the court at Vere. But in the lethal political web of the Veretian court, nothing is as it seems, and when Damen finds himself caught up in a play for the throne, he must work together with Laurent to survive and save his country.<br /><br />For Damen, there is just one rule: never, ever reveal his true identity. Because the one man Damen needs is the one man who has more reason to hate him than anyone else…<br /><br /><b>Includes an exclusive extra story!</b></span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/919874-hey-i-really-want-to-read-this-book-but-i">Hey! I really want to read this book but I have to ask first: Is this one of those books that &quot;romanticize&quot; rape and violence?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_919874'><a id="like_count_community_question_919874" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/919874?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">18 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F9305362-captive-prince">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/919874-hey-i-really-want-to-read-this-book-but-i">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/919874-hey-i-really-want-to-read-this-book-but-i">See all 17 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/5662657-shannon"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1591516451i/5662657._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/5662657-shannon">Shannon</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There is a difference in depiction of rape/violence and the romanticization of it. Unfortunately, some are not able to differentiate between the two. <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There is a difference in depiction of rape/violence and the romanticization of it. Unfortunately, some are not able to differentiate between the two. In the first book there are depictions present, but we view it through the lends of a character who is absolutely disgusted by it. Also, these are all actions by the royal upper-class, who as a whole are the villains of the trilogy. If depictions bother you as a reader, this probably isn't the series for you, but there is in no way any romanticization. <br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1565095368" />
    <a title="Maraia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8630441-maraia"><img alt="Maraia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480276982p2/8630441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1565095368?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maraia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maraia" href="/user/show/8630441-maraia">Maraia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425274262" href="/book/show/22571663-captive-prince">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8630441-maraia?shelf=g-adult-fantasy">g-adult-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8630441-maraia?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8630441-maraia?shelf=the-worst-of-the-worst">the-worst-of-the-worst</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1565095368" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13657806167349796818">Slavery isn’t sexy. Corporal punishment isn’t sexy. Rape isn’t sexy, and it certainly isn’t entertainment. This book is utterly disgusting.<br/><br/>There are so many things wrong with <i>Captive Prince</i>, it’s hard to know where to start. I’m having trouble understanding how this book can be praised by so many people, especially by those who promote LGBT relationships in books, consider themselves feminists, and are outspoken against violence against women being used as a plot device. <br/><br/>I love seeing LGBT relat</span>
  <span id="freeText13657806167349796818" style="display:none">Slavery isn’t sexy. Corporal punishment isn’t sexy. Rape isn’t sexy, and it certainly isn’t entertainment. This book is utterly disgusting.<br /><br />There are so many things wrong with <i>Captive Prince</i>, it’s hard to know where to start. I’m having trouble understanding how this book can be praised by so many people, especially by those who promote LGBT relationships in books, consider themselves feminists, and are outspoken against violence against women being used as a plot device. <br /><br />I love seeing LGBT relationships in books, but the characters in <i>Captive Prince</i> are either sex slave owners or sex slaves themselves. Personally, I don’t think that’s the kind of “relationship” we should be promoting, regardless of whether it’s LGBT or not. I fail to see how a book with graphic same sex rape scenes is beneficial to the “We Need Diverse Books” campaign. We need positive portrayals of LGBT characters, yes, but we don't need degrading ones. <br /><br />There has been a lot of criticism in recent years of gratuitous sexual violence against women in books, movies, and TV shows, as it is both offensive and harmful to the feminist movement. But apparently sexual violence is only a problem when directed against women, while it’s fine to have graphic scenes that serve no purpose other than to “entertain” the reader, as long as men are the ones getting raped? (Although how someone could find these scenes entertaining is beyond me.) When I define feminism, I think of women being valued as highly as men and being treated with as much respect — not more. <br /><br />Since I’ve seen people argue that the book isn’t <i>that</i> bad because the main character doesn’t actually get raped himself, I’d like to point out that <b>forced oral sex is still rape</b>. I’m not sure why this is such a hard concept, but my guess is that it’s connected to the fallacy that men can’t be raped in the first place. In <i>Captive Prince</i>, Damen has oral sex forced on him, and although he does have an orgasm, that doesn’t change the fact that, as a sex SLAVE, the act is in no way consensual. It is rape, any way you look at it. Orgasming does not equal consent, and that’s a dangerous idea to perpetuate. <br /><br />Rape isn’t the only thing trivialized by <i>Captive Prince</i>. I also find the portrayal of slavery quite offensive. As far as I can tell, all the kingdoms in C. S. Pacat’s world support slavery, and the slaves are used for sex. At one point, Damen compares slavery in his home country of Akielos to that in Vere, where he himself is a slave. According to him, slaves in Akielos know that they’re trading their personal freedom for “perfect treatment” by their masters, as if this somehow makes it okay. Not only that, but the life of a sex slave is glorified in the short story included in the paperback, which gives the background story of a minor character from the book. Claiming that slavery is “not that bad” because the slaves are “treated well,” they “enjoy their work,” and it’s “for their own good” is complete bullshit. That argument didn’t work when the U.S. had slaves, and it doesn’t work here. Just like rape is rape, slavery is slavery.<br /><br />The first two thirds of the book essentially has no plot, but instead features explicit rape scenes, alludes to even more, and throws in a beating or two to mix things up. All of a sudden, C. S. Pacat seemingly changes her mind and decides she wants to write a real fantasy novel, rather than rape erotica. At this point, the book actually does become captivating — the good kind. The potential for a solid fantasy is definitely there, I found the book hard to put down despite my revulsion, and I can see why people are quick to let themselves “forget” how the story starts. Unfortunately, no amount of engaging plot or world building can make up for the rape and sexual slavery in the first two thirds of the book, nor can a slave owner suddenly become a believable love interest for the slave. I’m assuming that’s where the story is headed, at least: Laurent has a tragic back story; he’s not really a bad guy, he’s just misunderstood; he doesn’t actually rape his slaves himself but lets others do the raping for him; he secretly has feelings for Damen, etc. Let’s stop right there. <b>Shipping Laurent and Damon is the equivalent of shipping a Nazi concentration camp guard with a Jewish prisoner.</b> I know this is a current trend in the romance genre, but how much (justified) outrage has there been at these novels? I fail to see how the upcoming “romance” in the Captive Prince trilogy is any different, and to be honest, I’m horrified by all the praise it has received. <br /><br />The fact that <i>Captive Prince</i> is being touted as a romance novel is the worst of a long list of faults and is incredibly insulting and insensitive to real victims of both rape and slavery. <br /><br />I’m giving this book one star, but only because zero stars would make it look as if I just forgot to rate it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13657806167349796818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1539437600" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1539437600" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1539437600?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1539437600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7932021133267694875">I don't read m/m fiction. It's not because I'm homophobic in any way (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6974899.Julio_Alexi_Genao' rel='nofollow noopener'>julio</a> would beat my ass down if I were), it's just that it's not a genre to which I gravitate. <br/><br/>For example, I don't read new adult. I don't read chick lit. I don't read m/m. It's simple as that. I prefer the romance in my books to be something that I can relate to, and I feel that for me, a romance would be more realistic if it's m/f. A book has to be completely amazing to change my mind about an m/m romance, and this book, wh</span>
  <span id="freeText7932021133267694875" style="display:none">I don't read m/m fiction. It's not because I'm homophobic in any way (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6974899.Julio_Alexi_Genao" rel="nofollow noopener">julio</a> would beat my ass down if I were), it's just that it's not a genre to which I gravitate. <br /><br />For example, I don't read new adult. I don't read chick lit. I don't read m/m. It's simple as that. I prefer the romance in my books to be something that I can relate to, and I feel that for me, a romance would be more realistic if it's m/f. A book has to be completely amazing to change my mind about an m/m romance, and this book, while not selling me on the genre, did a tremendous job of engaging my attention.<br /><br />This is due to the fact that <b>the character building is so amazing.</b> Let's make it clear, this book contains torture, sadism, rampant displays of sex - generally things that I don't care for, because despite my rampant use of profanity, I am a prude at heart. *blushes* Despite those facts, I really liked this book. The characters are so well-written.<br /><br />Damen is the Captive Prince. When his half-brother usurped the throne, he found himself a slave, shipped off to Vere. A prince, now a slave, he has to learn to completely change his personality, his will, his natural instincts, in order to be survive. He forces himself into submissiveness.<blockquote>
  <i>He knew what he had to do. Against every rebelling instinct, he forced himself forward, and dropped to his knees before Laurent.<br /><br />‘I fight in your service, Your Highness.’ He searched his memory for Radel’s words, and found them. ‘I exist only to please my Prince. May my victory reflect on your glory.’</i>
</blockquote>Laurent. Damn. What can I say about Laurent? Oh, how about the fact that <b>he makes Jericho-fucking-Barrons look like Prince Charming?</b><blockquote>
  <i>‘You look like a whore.’ The soft words barely stirred the air by Damen’s ear, inaudible to anyone else. Laurent murmured: ‘Filthy painted slut. Did you spread for my uncle the way you did for Kastor?’</i>
</blockquote>There are many words that can be used to describe Laurent. Words like <b>raging asshole, ginormous douchebag, sadistic motherfucker</b>, and other endearing phrases. The fact that I grew to like Laurent and sympathize with him is a testament to the author's skills.<br /><br />No, I will not be reading m/m all my days. No, I still do not enjoy rampant amounts of sex and debauchery, but I enjoyed this book, and that's enough.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7932021133267694875" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1357556742" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1357556742" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1357556742?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1357556742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16741655282370996151">For <a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk/category/romance/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Romance month at my blog</a>, I decided to take the opportunity to read something I wouldn't normally pick - this highly-praised M/M Fantasy Romance.<br/><br/>The first thing you should know: <b>this is a character-driven story</b>. I think you will enjoy it as long as you don't go into it expecting a lot of grand world-building. The focus of this book - indeed, the whole series, it would seem - is on the relationship between two men, and their relationships with other royals, guards and slaves around them.<br/><br/>As ro</span>
  <span id="freeText16741655282370996151" style="display:none">For <a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk/category/romance/" rel="nofollow noopener">Romance month at my blog</a>, I decided to take the opportunity to read something I wouldn't normally pick - this highly-praised M/M Fantasy Romance.<br /><br />The first thing you should know: <b>this is a character-driven story</b>. I think you will enjoy it as long as you don't go into it expecting a lot of grand world-building. The focus of this book - indeed, the whole series, it would seem - is on the relationship between two men, and their relationships with other royals, guards and slaves around them.<br /><br />As romances go, it has everything I could ask for:<br /><br />1) A really slow burn that makes a nice change from all the instant gratification NA romances I've read.<br />2) Characters that grow and develop with the plot.<br />3) Chemistry, both sexual and otherwise. Plus, a nice bit of hatred turned to reluctant partners in crime turned to...?<br /><br />The main story goes like this: Damen is a prince and the heir to the throne of Akielos. But when the king dies, Damen is captured and bundled off to Vere, disguised as a slave, while his half brother takes the throne. Vere is an enemy to Akielos and Damen must continue pretending to be a slave if he wishes to live.<br /><br />Enter Prince Laurent - heir to Vere and a pampered, spoiled and vindictive brat who becomes Damen's new master. Laurent is extremely unlikable at first, but Pacat manages to successfully grow him into a well-rounded and eventually likable character. <b>I loved how our perception of him changes gradually.</b><br /><br />Not surprisingly, the two princes despise each other at first. But what starts as an attempt to "break" one another, eventually becomes a reluctant partnership and a mutual understanding and respect.<br /><br />The book is quite dark at times and is definitely an adult novel. The romance in this first book is pretty much non-existent but the tension is set up nicely to deliver on that in the next two books. However, romance/sex aside, the book contains some graphic descriptions, floggings and rape scenes that could be upsetting for some readers.<br /><br />I enjoyed it, though, and will be picking up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17158513.Captive_Prince_Volume_Two__Captive_Prince___2_" title="Captive Prince Volume Two (Captive Prince, #2) by C.S. Pacat" rel="nofollow noopener">Captive Prince: Volume Two</a>.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/bookgeekreviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16741655282370996151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2047882993" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2047882993" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2047882993?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425274262" href="/book/show/22571663-captive-prince">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2047882993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3724304681505536783">I’m aware that <b>“Captive Prince”</b> is a highly controversial book and I know that many people have a lot of mixed feelings about it. As it seems you either hate it or you love it. There is no in-between. I think most of that is due to the fact that it deals with subjects we feel very uncomfortable with. Our modern minds have a tendency to shy away from those kinds of things, but just because a book makes you feel disgusted and angry, this still doesn’t automatically mean that it’s a bad book. Sure,</span>
  <span id="freeText3724304681505536783" style="display:none">I’m aware that <b>“Captive Prince”</b> is a highly controversial book and I know that many people have a lot of mixed feelings about it. As it seems you either hate it or you love it. There is no in-between. I think most of that is due to the fact that it deals with subjects we feel very uncomfortable with. Our modern minds have a tendency to shy away from those kinds of things, but just because a book makes you feel disgusted and angry, this still doesn’t automatically mean that it’s a bad book. Sure, C.S. Pacat confronts us with a lot of heavy topics. (And I’m not going to sugar-coat them!!! Just to make that perfectly clear!) There is rape, slavery, sexual abuse, torture, violence and even the mention of paedophilia. Just to name a few of them and there are scenes that no doubt will revolt you immensely. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[For instance the moment with Ancel and Damen in the gardens!!! I’ll never ever be okay with that scene!!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><b>BUT</b><br><br>In contrast to the generally prevailing opinion, she always touches those delicate subjects with care. Well at least with as much care as is possible in such a book… In my subjective opinion she doesn’t glorify the conditions of the pets and slaves at Vere’s court and she definitely doesn’t sympathize with their tormentors. I think the fact we see everything through Damen’s eyes, the eyes of a mistreated slave, is testimonial enough that C.S. Pacat is not okay with the things that happen to the slaves in the book! <br><br><i>You are permanently disgusted by us, aren't you?" said Laurent.</i><br><br>I guess that quote says it all! So yes, I do get why the topics in this book rub people the wrong way and I know that “Captive Prince” might not be for everyone. I still want you to keep in mind that things like that are nothing new though. Throughout the long history of mankind those subjects have always been a part of our lives. There were plenty of wars and people have always been tortured, raped, abused and enslaved! Damn it! Who am I kidding? Things like that still happen all around the world. Just take a closer look at other countries (or even your own) and you’ll know what I mean. So yeah, I think what I want to say is that C.S. Pacat shouldn’t be blamed for mentioning those topics, because for some people they were actually reality (ancient Rome and Greece instantly come to mind) and in fact still are a part of some people’s reality. We should neither forget that nor ignore it. Whilst it’s true that Pacat sometimes has a tendency to exaggerate excessively and easily slips into clichés that doesn’t mean that all parts of the historical accuracy are wrong. ;-) The author obviously aims to provoke and we are supposed to feel uncomfortable when we read her book. I can only speak for myself but in my case it definitely worked. <br><br>Well, this said I’m glad that the world in Pacat’s book is just fictional and that I can finally get to the fun part: My actual review! <br><br><b>The plot:</b><br><br>Betrayed by his own brother and shipped into the lands of his enemies Prince Damianos of Akielos ends up in the foreign land of Vere. Brought as a gift for Prince Laurent he is supposed to be the young heir’s pleasure slave, a role that revolts Damen immensely and makes it exceptionally difficult to keep a low profile. Powerless and enslaved he has no other choice than to obey though, his hope to find a way to escape the only thing that helps him to endure. As long as no one knows about his true identity he has a chance at survival…. But sooner or later someone is bound to find out that he’s not who he claims to be. Will Damen be able to escape the corrupt court of Vere or will someone blow his cover before he even gets a decent chance to flee? <br><br>I know the story sounds so cliché and cheesy! And in fact it is! But damn did I enjoy this reread! *lol* I think it’s because I know what’s coming in the next two books and to be aware of the plot made this reread such an interesting experience. I noticed so many things I didn’t see the first time around and I have to give Pacat kudos for dropping so many subtle hints. XD I think she didn’t really know what she wanted to achieve with the first book and mainly aimed to shock her audience, but boy does it get better in “Prince’s Gambit”. <br>Anyway, let’s head to the characters section! I can’t wait to gush about those two! *lol*<br><br><b>The characters:</b><br><br><b>Damen – The pleasure slave</b><br><br><i>”Why not?” said Damen. “I don’t share your craven habit of hitting only those who cannot hit back, and I take no pleasure in hurting those weaker than myself.” Driven past reason, the words came out in his own language.</i><br><br>I feel soo damn sorry for what happens to him in this book! He doesn’t deserve any of the things that happen to him (not that anyone would ever deserve such things!!) and he’s such a precious and innocent soul. Even enslaved and in the hands of the enemy he still tries everything possible in order to help his people and to remain true to himself. No matter what happens to him, he always does what he thinks is right and if that means that he’ll take a beating for his convictions and beliefs he still goes through with it! I love that about him! He’s brave and honourable and at the corrupt and thoroughly tainted court of Vere to be like that is actually more than just an achievement! XD<br><br><i>”He wanted to face Kastor, his brother, and ask him, man to man, why he had done what he had done. But life in Akielos went on without Damianos. These slaves had no one else to help them.<br>And what did it mean, to be a prince, if he did not strive to protect those weaker than himself?”</i><br><br><i>”This place sickened him. Anywhere else, you simply killed your enemy with a sword. Or poisoned him, if you had the honourless instincts of an assassin. Here, it was layer upon layer of constructed double-dealing, dark, polished and unpleasant.”</i><br><br><b>Laurent – The cast-iron bitch</b><br><br><i>”Laurent was indeed good at talking. He accepted sympathy gracefully. He put his position rationally. He stopped the flow of talk when it became dangerously critical of his uncle. He said nothing that could be taken as an open slight on the Regency. Yet no one who talked to him could have any doubt that his uncle was behaving at best misguidedly and at worst treasonously.”</i><br><br>Oh Laurent! My ruthless and poisonous “nest of scorpions”! He’s so damn cruel and obnoxious in this book, I can totally see why everyone hates him! *lol* My weird and crazy mind always likes a good villain though so it’s no surprise I actually ended up loving him. XD Laurent is such a complex and well-thought-out character, it’s a pleasure to read about all his cunning and almost artful schemes. Well, at least for me it was. I know one of my fellow buddy readers hated him fiercely! Haha! ;-P The prince of Vere isn’t all controlled anger and hate though; he has a soft side too. Admittedly we really don’t see a lot of it in the first book (which actually is the reason why it’s the weakest and worst book of the entire series) but since I know that this is going to change I really can’t wait to read book two. And yes, I admit it: Laurent’s cunning and strategical mind is sexy! Don’t blame me, just like Damen I stand by my opinion. ;-)<br><br><i>”I’ll offer for you, if you like. When the time comes. I wouldn’t want you in my bed, but you’d have all the same privileges. You might prefer that. I’d offer.”</i><br><br><i>Laurent went very still; then he deliberately shifted in his seat and leaned in, bringing his lips right to Damen’s ear. “I think I’m out of stabbing range, he’s got short arms. Or perhaps he’ll try to throw a sugarplum? That <b>is</b> difficult. If I duck, he’ll hit Torveld.”</i><br><br><i>Laurent took it without saying anything. He tucked it carefully into a fold of his riding clothes. Then after a moment, he reached out, and touched Nicaise’s chin with one knuckle. <br>“You look better without all the paint,” said Laurent.</i><br><br><b>Nicaise – The pet</b><br><br><i>”I don’t need you. He’s promised. He’s not going to give me up.” Nicaise’s voice was smug and self-satisfied.<br>“He gives them all up,” said Laurent, “even if you’re more enterprising than the others have been.”</i><br><br>I will always have a soft spot for Nicaise. I know he’s bitchy and at least as insufferable as Laurent, I can’t help but like him though. When it comes down to it, he’s just a product of his environment and he’s still so very young. I hate and despise the Regent for choosing him as his pet and the thought of them together makes me feel sick to my stomach. &gt;_&lt; It’s obvious Nicaise and Laurent care about each other deeply, yet they have no other choice than to play by the Regent’s rules. Poor, young and innocent Nicaise… Urgh… he was 10 when he started to serve the Regent… 10 for Christ’s sake!!! I’ll never get over that! <br><br><i>”Don’t underestimate him because of his age. He has experienced things many adults have not, and his mind is no longer that of a child. Though even a child may learn how to manipulate an adult.”</i><br><br><i>”He ordered everyone out of his apartments. I wouldn’t try to see him.”<br>“Why not?” Nicaise said. He looked past Damen towards Laurent’s chamber. “What happened? Is he all right?”</i><br><br><b>The Regent – Mr. I-freaking-hate-him-so-much</b><br><br><i>”Do you think it pleases me to discipline my own nephew? No uncle acts with a heavier heart. Shoulder your responsibilities – ride to Delfeur – show me you have even a drop fo your brother’s blood and I will joyfully restore it all.”</i><br><br>Did anyone of you ever notice that the people of Vere always consider the Akielons to be barbaric and brute? Considering what I saw of the Regents court I’d rather say it’s the other way around!! They hide behind their sophisticated demeanour and their complicated clothes but in fact they are the true barbarians of the story, none more so than the Regent himself!!! I despise and hate that man so much and I truly hope he burns in the nine circles of hell. Come to think of it, his actions might easily cause him to end up in all of them. *lol* So yes, the Regent is a villain I hate with a fierce passion and I can’t wait for him to get what he deserves!!! *grrrr*<br><br><i>”Why must you always defy me? I hate it when we are at odds, yet you force me to chastise you. You seem determined to wreck everything in your path. Blessed with gifts, you squander them. Given opportunities, you waste them. I hate to see you grown up like this,” said the Regent, “when you were such a lovely boy.”</i><br><br>This said, I really enjoyed my re-read and I can’t wait to see the “true Laurent” in the next book! XD I think what made this even more fun was the fact that it was a buddy read with my two lovely girls! My adorable <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/66222749-lia-bonnibel" rel="nofollow noopener">Gansey</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10675488-swaye" rel="nofollow noopener">mo mhuirnín</a> kept me entertained with their different opinions (and their strong emotions *lol*) and it was such a pleasure to be able to discuss this book! =) <br><br>I can’t wait to dive into “Prince’s Gambit”! ;-) Now it’s finally getting cute and nice! &lt;3<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1516869249i/24918661._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3724304681505536783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer451122351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13856101020633311676"><b>*ONLY $1.99 TODAY AT AMAZON US! This is not a drill! 9/3/19 <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.amazon.com/Captive-Prince-Trilogy-ebook/dp/B00I3REIHI/'>https://www.amazon.com/Captive-Prince...</a>*</b><br/><br/>This book owned me today, completely owned me.<br/><br/>I just have to give S. U. Pacat a huge round of applause. I was 100% drawn into "Captive Prince". It is going to be hard to write a review of just Volume 1 because I read them back to back like a rabid fan-girl so I'll just review them together. It was like my eyes were glued to my phone today. I wouldn't and couldn't stop reading. <br/><br/>I won't rehash the </span>
  <span id="freeText13856101020633311676" style="display:none"><b>*ONLY $1.99 TODAY AT AMAZON US! This is not a drill! 9/3/19 <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.amazon.com/Captive-Prince-Trilogy-ebook/dp/B00I3REIHI/">https://www.amazon.com/Captive-Prince...</a>*</b><br /><br />This book owned me today, completely owned me.<br /><br />I just have to give S. U. Pacat a huge round of applause. I was 100% drawn into "Captive Prince". It is going to be hard to write a review of just Volume 1 because I read them back to back like a rabid fan-girl so I'll just review them together. It was like my eyes were glued to my phone today. I wouldn't and couldn't stop reading. <br /><br />I won't rehash the plot because the overview doesn't sound terribly interesting or new. It is the masterful, smart writing that sets this book apart. The writing is so crisp and fan-freaking-tastic that it gives each word the power that it is due. Details sing in all the right ways. <br /><br />The way the author portrayed Laurent in the beginning made me think I could never sympathize with him. It is through truly skilled writing that little facts play out just as they should over time and reveal Laurent's character in new lights. We learn hard truths along with Damen and I felt my point of view morphing as his did. I was entwined with Damen and felt deeply connected to his story and his emotional and physical journey. <br /><br />The book is a study in deception and human emotion. It grips you until the very end. Book 1 set the stage for book 2, which just brings everything to a head. There are no missteps. It is like a ballet dance of words, and I don't think I'm being too complementary or over-exaggerating. Book 3 will be my most anticipated release of next year (if that is when it will come out)!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17663155863974633176"><b>This might get -a tad- salty.</b><br/><br/>Well... I don’t know what the fuck to make of this book but suffice it to say I finally understand why many find it polarising. <br/><br/>The characters were boring and one-dimensional as shit. The plot was profoundly lacking. Or more like, there was NONE. What the fuck is a story without a well rounded, well constructed plot anyway? And if you can’t deliver on a good plot at least have some interesting characters to keep the reader engaged. <br/>This was just... please excuse my l</span>
  <span id="freeText17663155863974633176" style="display:none"><b>This might get -a tad- salty.</b><br /><br />Well... I don’t know what the fuck to make of this book but suffice it to say I finally understand why many find it polarising. <br /><br />The characters were boring and one-dimensional as shit. The plot was profoundly lacking. Or more like, there was NONE. What the fuck is a story without a well rounded, well constructed plot anyway? And if you can’t deliver on a good plot at least have some interesting characters to keep the reader engaged. <br />This was just... please excuse my language but fucking and/or raping. Or fantasying about fucking and raping. <br />I did not sign up for this shit. <br /><br />A lot of the explicit scenes were so incredibly unnecessary. Too unnecessary. <br />I understand the need to inform us the basics and inner machinations of the court politics to set the scene for how they treat their (sex) slaves and whatnot but all the rest was just like, okay, I get it: They’re fucking demented. Now how about you give me a plot or story to work with other than THAT! <br /><br />Oh, and by the way, sex with a 13-year-old is called Paedophilia for fuck’s sake. And rape. No other word for it. <br />Sorry if I’m not “getting what the book is really about”. What the hell was it about anyway? I still don’t get it. <br /><br />And lastly, apologies for the overuse of the F word. I’m just feeling very cheated right now.<br />I’m told books two and three knock it out of the park so, see we shall. <br /><br /><b>What I did like:</b><br /><br />Damen. </span>

<div id="review_689239825" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/689239825" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/689239825?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17158549-captive-prince">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=rich-guys">rich-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dangerous-hero-themed-books-read">dangerous-hero-themed-books-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=forbidden-romance">forbidden-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=hate-that-i-love-them">hate-that-i-love-them</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=kidnapped">kidnapped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dom-sub-bdsm">dom-sub-bdsm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dark-themes">dark-themes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer689239825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2599367806310709168">'Captive Prince' has been on my radar for a long time now. I have seen a plethora of glowing reviews from friends that have loved this series. As curious as I was, I kept putting off reading this series because M/M reads aren't really my thing. However, my curiosity finally got the best of me and I downloaded the first audiobook in the series. <br/><br/>The rest is history! I blew through all three audiobooks in a couple of days, listening to them back to back until I had devoured the entire series. This </span>
  <span id="freeText2599367806310709168" style="display:none">'Captive Prince' has been on my radar for a long time now. I have seen a plethora of glowing reviews from friends that have loved this series. As curious as I was, I kept putting off reading this series because M/M reads aren't really my thing. However, my curiosity finally got the best of me and I downloaded the first audiobook in the series. <br /><br />The rest is history! I blew through all three audiobooks in a couple of days, listening to them back to back until I had devoured the entire series. This series was fantastic!<br /><br />Since I finished all three books in the series before sitting down to write my reviews, I'll do my best not to give any big spoilers. The specifics of where one book ended and the next began are a little hazy for me. However, they were all worthwhile and highly entertaining books.<br /><br />'Captive Prince: Volume One', introduces us to Damen and Laurent. The two are princes from rival kingdoms, only Damen's true identity is a secret to everyone in Laurent's court. If his true identity were known, he would surely be executed. Damen is surrounded by enemies, betrayed by his half-brother and sold into slavery.<br /><br />Although the two are enemies, Damen and Laurent have many things in common. Both princes have fallen prey to family members who want to seize their crowns. Damen had his rule usurped by his illegitimate half-brother, Kastor, while Laurent is at the mercy of his uncle, who rules in his stead until Laurent is old enough to claim his crown. <br /><br />That being said, it is hard to envision Laurent in the role of a victim. From the first introduction, his manipulative, and often cruel, nature is apparent. His treatment of Damen is deplorable as he strives to assert his power over his new, wild and unbroken pleasure slave. Laurent is clearly a character that enjoys head games.<br /><br />On the other hand, Damen is a character that has instant appeal. He is put in an unspeakable situation and betrayed by the brother that he looked up to. My heart went out to Damen. I wanted to see him prevail.<br /><br />Upon Damen's arrival in the Vere, he is thrown into a life of debauchery. The Verethian court is filled with hedonistic and taboo sexual activities. The members of the courts indulge in every depraved act you can imagine. Nothing is off-limits, with the exception of enjoying pleasure slaves of the opposite gender in an effort to prevent the conception of illegitimate children that would sully the Verethian bloodlines. Rape and pedophilia are a way of life.<br /><br />Accordingly, this will not be a book for many readers. It is full of dark, controversial and offensive content. This is not a lovey dovey type of story AT ALL. You will be appalled.<br /><br />In fact, that is a large part of the appeal of this story. There aren't too many graphic sex acts depicted, but the constant lingering threat of rape gives this book a very ominous feeling. I spent the entire time on the edge of my seat, waiting for the assault that I knew was inevitable. The anticipation, and resulting anxiety, was immense.<br /><br />For most of this book, Laurent portrays a spoiled, bratty and cruel prince. He treats Damen harshly and is extremely abusive. However, there are brief glimpses of another side of him. I have no doubt that there is far more to Laurent than meets the eye.<br /><br />This book definitely had my rapt attention. It wasn't like most of the books that I read, but I was completely hooked. Without missing a beat, I dived right into the second book to continue Damen and Laurent's story.<br /><br />Check out more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookaddicthaven.com">www.bookaddicthaven.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2599367806310709168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=dark">dark</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=excruciating">excruciating</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1942116707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13533357836213553652"><b>TRIGGER WARNINGS ALERT </b> Stay away from this one if you prefer safe reads. Don't read my review if the word "rape" makes you unconfortable, because I use it a lot, because this book has a lot of that.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489552373ra/22225459.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I don't recommend this if you feel uncomfortable reading about:<br/><br/><b> Pedophilia </b><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Nicasius is only 13 and he's used as a sex slave. The worst is that he is supposed to be willing to be forever a sex slave because the king, his master, gets tired of children when they grow up and Nicasious is</span></span>
  <span id="freeText13533357836213553652" style="display:none"><b>TRIGGER WARNINGS ALERT </b> Stay away from this one if you prefer safe reads. Don't read my review if the word "rape" makes you unconfortable, because I use it a lot, because this book has a lot of that.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489552373ra/22225459.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I don't recommend this if you feel uncomfortable reading about:<br><br><b> Pedophilia </b><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Nicasius is only 13 and he's used as a sex slave. The worst is that he is supposed to be willing to be forever a sex slave because the king, his master, gets tired of children when they grow up and Nicasious is eagerly searching for a new master. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b> Rape and Sexual violence </b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Damianos the Main character is entered in a slave contest where the loser gets raped. He gets drugged by Laurent "his love interest" so that he'll get weakened and lose the contest and Laurent can watch when Damianos gets raped...publicily!! In this book the court takes rape as a sport. Later Damiano's forced to receive oral sex from another slave to the enjoyment of Laurent. I repeat, Laurent is the "love interest".  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b> No romance </b><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ by the end of the book there's not even a kiss  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b> Stockholm Syndrome </b><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Erasmus, A sexual slave, gets raped all the time but he supposedly enjoys being a sex pet and is all grateful when he gets to serve another master because said master treats sex-slaves "better". Sorry but in what sick world a sex-slave enjoys being a slave?How is that romantic or sexy?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><b> Extreme violence </b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Laurent, the MC "love interest", is a Prince and he gives orders to whip Damianos. This is vividly described and Damianos spends some time recovering from his injuries. How is that romantic? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b> Double standards </b> So Christian Grey gets the sh*t here in GR although he NEVER raped ANA, (although, to be honest he pushed her consent, but NEVER raped her) yet Laurent gets nothing but praise??? So dubious consent, sexual violence, and rape are okay when the characters are male? NO JUST NO!! That's not feminist at all, that's not fair. If the main character had been Princess Damiana everyone and their dog would be screaming murder. "Oh the abusive relationship in romance!" But because the victim is a male then it's okay? How is that fair? <br><br><b>Unsafe reads </b> This is supposedly a slow-burn-romance between two males, but there's a lot of cheating and disloyalty. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ In the sequel of this rape -fest Laurent who is Damianos owner and master, "lends" Damianos to a group of women warriors so that they can use him for reproductive purposes. Laurent's not even slightly jealous! He laughs with joy when Damianos returns to their tent worn-out from having sex with a lot of women in just one night. Damianos is attracted to Laurent but he is more attracted to women than to males. So we the readers don't get a little bit of cute jealousy and the couple doesn't kiss until way into the second book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I'm not the most articulated, coherent reviewer, so I invite you to read these reviews if you want more info on the problematic issues of this book.<br><br> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1559280522" rel="nofollow noopener">Cait's review</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1609350685" rel="nofollow noopener">Lainey's review</a><br><br>This book makes me angry. The writing is exquisite and clever, but it's the most disgusting portrayal of an M/M relationship. <b> Contrary to what this book portrays, Homosexual Men have healthy, committed relationships </b>. This is not the best book to portray diverse couples, because, as it is, a lot of people think wrongly that homosexuality and bisexuality are against nature and that Bisexuals and Homosexual aren't capable of loving, committed relationships. This book only re-inforces the idea of sexually "degenerated" characters. In real life gay people aren't like this. Not at all.<br><br> I gave two stars to the sequel because the graphic rapes aren't present. It's cleverly written and it's addictive, but it's still a harsh read because poor Nicaise. It's not fair what happened to him.<br><br>Final note: There are reviewers here in GR who praise this book to no end, and yet get all angry and write rants about romances like Twilight, Hopeless, FSOG, Beautiful disaster and other romance books of the romance genre. At time it feels like some of those reviewers are trying to make the people who enjoy, for example, FSOG bad with themselves because "they are supporting a book that portrays an abusive relationship". Yet they go and praise this very abusive book. <br><br>This isn't about me having a problem with the people who like this book. I think it's okay if people enjoy this kind of books because<br><br>* Everyone has different tastes and opinions and all opinions are equally valid. You enjoy this book? That's fine.<br> * WE ALL ARE SMART! WE ALL KNOW HOW TO DIFFERENTIATE REALITY FROM BOOKS. We all know that In real life rape is wrong. The people who love this book to death aren't supporters of rape, this is just a book. But just like the the captive prince fanbase knows the difference between reality and books, the FSOG fanbase knows better than go and get themselves in abusive relationships because of a book.<br><br>My problem is when the double standard comes:<b>Contrary to popular GR belief the people who enjoy books that portray abusive M/F relationships are as smart as the people who enjoys Captive prince.</b> Just saying. <br><br>So anyone who enjoys FSOG or any other bad-reviewed romance, but never says it aloud for fear of how their opinion will make them look in a site like GR where people trash "abusive relationship" books, should say it aloud. Most of FSOG bashers are top reviewers who praise this rape-fest so there's nothing wrong with liking FSOG or any other poorly-reviewed romance. <br><br>If you like me feel unconfortable reading certain topics, ignore most of the 5 star reviews, very few of them mention the problematic issues of this book and most lack trigger warnings. Read some 3 stars reviews and some triggers warnings before deciding if this book is for you or not.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9567299957538535586">okay. well. its not too difficult to figure out why this book isnt for everyone and i completely understand why its so polarising. <br/><br/>there are so many sensitive and taboo topics, but i dont think its done distastefully. this is seriously the slowest of slow burns, and i think thats important. had the relationship between damen and laurent developed more quickly, it probably would have been off-putting. <br/><br/>as far as the story goes, its intriguing and unlike anything i have read before. there is a nice</span>
  <span id="freeText9567299957538535586" style="display:none">okay. well. its not too difficult to figure out why this book isnt for everyone and i completely understand why its so polarising. <br /><br />there are so many sensitive and taboo topics, but i dont think its done distastefully. this is seriously the slowest of slow burns, and i think thats important. had the relationship between damen and laurent developed more quickly, it probably would have been off-putting. <br /><br />as far as the story goes, its intriguing and unlike anything i have read before. there is a nice balance between world building and introducing court/power dynamics, which helps provide substance for the plot. however, some parts were a little too slow for my liking. but overall, not a bad read and im sufficiently hooked!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1330487277" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1330487277" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1330487277?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425274262" href="/book/show/22571663-captive-prince">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2015">year-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1330487277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4753613560829760984"><b>Holy. Shit. Folks.</b><br/><br/>I was so <u>disappointed</u> in this book. <br/><br/>I've been meaning to write a review for this for a while because there is an <b>OVERWHELMING</b> amount of positivity surrounding the series and I just... <br/><br/><i>WHY???</i><br/><br/>The plot was vapid beyond belief. The first 3/4 of the story goes practically nowhere and is made up of lots of weird sex and torture. <br/><br/>Contrived elements that were meant to make you feel desperation & sadness? They only succeeded in making me feel bitter and unconvinced. <br/><br/><b>The big reveal at th</b></span>
  <span id="freeText4753613560829760984" style="display:none"><b>Holy. Shit. Folks.</b><br /><br />I was so <u>disappointed</u> in this book. <br /><br />I've been meaning to write a review for this for a while because there is an <b>OVERWHELMING</b> amount of positivity surrounding the series and I just... <br /><br /><i>WHY???</i><br /><br />The plot was vapid beyond belief. The first 3/4 of the story goes practically nowhere and is made up of lots of weird sex and torture. <br /><br />Contrived elements that were meant to make you feel desperation &amp; sadness? They only succeeded in making me feel bitter and unconvinced. <br /><br /><b>The big reveal at the end was predictable and totally dissatisfying.</b><br /><br />Now let me just mention here that there are many sexual encounters in this novel <u>but it seems that in most scenarios there is at least 1 unwilling party involved.</u><br /><br />And that's what bothers me... this is supposed to be a romance???<br /><br />There was hardly anything sexy going on here, and the strange interactions between our two main characters honestly had me laughing out loud (in a "laughing at you, not with you" kind of way.)<br /><br />I've seen many reviews calling it a "slow burn" romance but I felt zero chemistry between our two princes. <b>ZERO.</b><br /><br />The other outstandingly terrible feature of this novel was the writing. <br /><br />Oh my god. <br /><br />Did the author have her face buried in a thesaurus to try and make her writing seem more sophisticated?? It felt like she went through and found the <b>MOST OBSCURE</b> synonym and slapped it haphazardly into a sentence. <br /><br /><i>"Sentence enhancers, right Patrick??"</i><br /><br />I have a decently stocked vocabulary, but these words were completely out of left field and interrupted the flow of the sentence. <b>It's not cute. It makes your writing sound like it's trying too hard.</b><br /><br />When I tried to return this book<i>
  <b>Amazon didn't even want it back...</b>
</i><br /><br />I'm afraid I will not be able to understand all the high praise this book is receiving. <br /><br />I have no interest in what happens next, as I didn't even read the sneak preview of the sequel. I was excited to read a m/m love story with a medieval essence <b>but all I found here was a boring foray into absurdity.</b><br /><br /><i>***P.S. 10 points to anyone who got my Spongebob reference before reaching the end.***</i><br /><br /><i>***P.S. x2 I did actually end up reading the second book in this series and you can find my review <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1796948070?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> if you love a good weenie roast!***</i></span>

<div id="review_1537690161" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1537690161" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1537690161?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20878022-captive-prince">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=half-fantasy">half-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=riddikulus">riddikulus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=made-me-lose-my-damn-mind">made-me-lose-my-damn-mind</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=i-have-rules">i-have-rules</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=jerk-of-my-dreams">jerk-of-my-dreams</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=here-be-slaves">here-be-slaves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=that-bastard">that-bastard</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=shiny">shiny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=diabolical">diabolical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1537690161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2830721827840636736"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2016/02/review-captive-prince-by-c-s-pacat-jessicadhaluska.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/>If you haven't been seeing/hearing the buzz surrounding THE CAPTIVE PRINCE by C.S. Pacat, you've probably been living under a rock. I'd seen it EVERYWHERE, even before one of my favorite authors recommended it in her newsletter (<------why I finally caved).<br/><br/>My impression before reading it was that it was some kind of pseudo-fantasy/MM/BDSM mashup . . . and that impression was fairly accurate.<br/><br/>Not my typical choice of reading material, but HYPE. And CURIOSITY. *shakes fist a</span>
  <span id="freeText2830721827840636736" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2016/02/review-captive-prince-by-c-s-pacat-jessicadhaluska.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>If you haven't been seeing/hearing the buzz surrounding THE CAPTIVE PRINCE by C.S. Pacat, you've probably been living under a rock. I'd seen it EVERYWHERE, even before one of my favorite authors recommended it in her newsletter (&lt;------why I finally caved).<br><br>My impression before reading it was that it was some kind of pseudo-fantasy/MM/BDSM mashup . . . and that impression was fairly accurate.<br><br>Not my typical choice of reading material, but HYPE. And CURIOSITY. *shakes fist at curiosity gods* <br><br>As one might guess from the title (if one pays attention to things like titles *shakes fist at self*), the MC of this tale is a prince (Damen) made captive . . . A prince given as a sex slave to the prince and heir (Laurent) of a rival kingdom, only they don't <i>know</i> he's a prince, but that's a good thing, b/c Damen did a really, really Bad Thing in the last war, and if Laurent found out Damen was actually the REAL Damen, and not just <i>called</i> "Damen" b/c Kastor (Damen's illegitimate usurping half-brother) thought Laurent would be amused by having a sex slave named for the man he most hates in the world . . . Well, that would be Bad.<br><br>Did all of that cross your eyes? B/c as convoluted as it sounds, it's deceptively simple.<br><br>What <i>isn't</i> simple is everything that came after the initial introductions, and how I feel about it. <br><br>Obviously, as a prince, Damen isn't too keen on becoming a sex slave. But who cares? B/c sex slave. <br><br>And even though there technically wasn't much sex (on page), the hedonistic attitude of the nobility permeated the atmosphere, and the threat was constant, like background noise. And YES . . . I do mean <i>threat</i>. <br><br>But in that weird, willful suspension of disbelief way that's exciting even as you're consciously uncomfortable. <br><br>Enter Nicaise, the thirteen-year-old "pet" of a dirty old man in Laurent's court. The thirteen-year-old who's been serving in his role as "pet" for THREE YEARS. Who is maneuvering to keep his position, b/c he knows--EVERYONE knows--that he has maybe another year before he outgrows his master's tastes. <br><br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/657106.gif" width="350" height="263" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br><b>So there are two things you need to know before picking up this book:</b><br><br>1. There's rape.<br>2. There's pedophilia.<br><br>I almost stopped 20% in, when Nicaise first showed up. I'm not sure what kept me going. Could've been the remnants of curiosity. Could've been the person who made an asinine comment on one of my status updates about how pedophilia isn't being endorsed by the book, which pissed me off enough to make me <i>want</i> to finish it, all the better to KILL IT WITH FIRE. B/c really? Show me a book that <i>does</i> endorse the sexual violation of children, and I'll show you a jail cell. #GTFO<br><br>Either way, I kept going. <br><br>And much to my chagrin, I found myself fascinated by Laurent. <br><br>He's a prince with the foul mouth of a tavern brawler. Hatred burns in his eyes, but he almost always maintains a perfect calmness that is infuriating. He's a brilliant manipulator who superficially appears to be no more than an indulged royal brat.<br><br>Beyond my newfound obsession with Laurent, I was reading not only to try to understand my prince, but in anticipation of other (despicable) characters' downfalls. <br><br>So I'm hooked. *shrugs awkwardly*<br><br>But if I'd known what I was getting into, I'd never have started. <br><br>A secondary issue was the thinly veiled attempt to elevate the book above the stereotypes of its genre.<br><br>I have an extensive vocabulary. I majored in English, but even if I hadn't, you can't read as much as I do and not pick up an impressive number of words along the way.<br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455460412i/18105135.jpg" width="500" height="375" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>#thestruggleisreal<br><br>Even so, it's not unusual for me to make use of the handy, dandy word lookup feature found on all ereaders.<br><br>What <i>is</i> unusual is having to use said lookup feature every few pages. <br><br>It took awhile to catch on, so I missed the early ones, but after I grew wise to the tactic, I began highlighting: <i>appurtenances</i>, <i>peripatetic</i>, <i>damascened</i>, <i>febrile</i>, <i>machicolation</i>, etc.<br><br>I could go on . . . and on . . . and <i>on</i>.<br><br>After I acclimated to the overuse of words rarely (if ever) found . . . anywhere, I began to notice that many of them were frou frou stand-ins for more common words and phrases. <br><br>A man didn't frown. His "<i>smooth brow <b>corrugated</b></i>."<br><br>A room wasn't ostentatious, it was, "<i><b>afroth</b> with ornament</i>."<br><br>I was pretty sure "afroth" wasn't a real word. I was further convinced when the word lookup yielded no results. BUT. Word lookup isn't infallible, so I googled it . . . And discovered that it <i>was</i> a real word, but had been misused. Unless Pacat intended to say the ornaments in the room were, "<i>in a state of lively or angry excitement</i>."<br><br>[Afroth." Merriam-Webster.com. Merriam-Webster, n.d. Web. 6 Feb. 2016.]<br><br>I usually applaud the Shakespearean tactic of adapting, evolving, <i>creating</i> words to suit your purposes . . . <br><br>BUT.<br><br>In this case, it felt disingenuous. <br><br>Like the author had hangups about the type of book she was writing--SMUT. Maybe intelligent SMUT, but still SMUT--and decided to overcompensate by impressing her readers with her intelligence and/or education via the implementation of obscure words that none of us have ever heard of.<br><br>Instead, it provided a distraction, b/c constantly having to lookup words. <br><br>SO. THE CAPTIVE PRINCE by C.S. Pacat is a <i>deeply</i> flawed book, despite its low page count. If you can handle rape and sexual exploitation as abhorrent cultural practices, then you, too, should willingly fling yourself into this deep, dark hole. If you can't, RUN AWAY. If you don't, you'll probably find yourself as entangled as I am, but you've been forewarned, so you'll have only yourself to blame. <br><br>BUT.<br><br>If book 2 isn't the significant improvement I'm promised . . . Heads. Will. ROLL. <br><br><b>SPOILERY final thoughts:</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Unless Pacat is laying false trails, I think it's pretty obvious that Regent orchestrated the deaths of both Laurent's father (the King) and older brother. Both Damen and Laurent believe their side was the one betrayed by the other, and that REEKS of a puppet master. <br><br>ALSO, the second Nicaise was revealed to be Regent's pet, it made sense both why Regent didn't just kill Laurent as well, and why Laurent has such violent reactions to the strong taking advantage of the weak.<br><br>Despicable. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425274262" href="/book/show/22571663-captive-prince">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to destiny ♡⚔♡ by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/7772979-jue">Jue.</a>
  </div>
